{% endccb %}

# What is it?

This appears to be brainfuck code, and it is also way too long to read manually. When the program is run, it just outputs `Wrong!`

# Overview

Find some patterns in the code, that can mark significant segments (most of the program has to be icing, right?)

We then run small segments of code then look at the memory to see the result

[This interpreter](https://copy.sh/brainfuck/) was used

# Reading code

First we figure out what the commands in brainfuck are:


>	increment pointer

<	decrement pointer

+	increment value at pointer

-	decrement value at pointer

[	begin loop (continues while value at pointer is non-zero)

]	end loop

,	read one character from input into value at pointer

.	print value at pointer to output as a character


Some of the long chains of < or > are hard to read, so we made a python script to, instead, show the current pointer as p`  ` before every operation:

{% ccb lang:py scrollable:true gutter1:1-19 %}
e = open("brainfix.txt", 'r')
j = e.read()
pointer = 0
list2 = []
pointermode = False
for i in range(len(j)):
    if j[i] != "<" and j[i] != ">":
        if pointermode:
            list2.append("p" + str(pointer))
            pointermode = False
        list2.append(j[i])
    else:
        pointermode = True
        if j[i] == "<":
            pointer-= 1
        if j[i] == ">":
            pointer+= 1
e.close()
print("".join(list2))
{% endccb %}

The output:

{% ccb caption:brainfixed.txt wrapped:true scrollable:true %}

{% endccb %}

We see a notable segment at the end:

{% ccb caption:censorship wrapped:true scrollable:true %}
p4[-]p5[-]p7[-]p8[-]p9[-]p10[-]p11[-]p12[-]p13[-]p14[-]p15[-]p16[-]p17[-]p18[-]p19[-]p20[-]p21[-]p22[-]p23[-]p24[-]p25[-]p26[-]p27[-]p28[-]p29[-]p30[-]p31[-]p32[-]p33[-]p34[-]p35[-]p36[-]p37[-]p38[-]p39[-]p40[-]p41[-]p42[-]p43[-]p44[-]p45[-]p46[-]p47[-]p48[-]p49[-]p50[-]p51[-]p52[-]p53[-]p54[-]p55[-]p56[-]p57[-]p58[-]p59[-]p60[-]p61[-]p62[-]p63[-]p64[-]p65[-]p66[-]p67[-]p68[-]p69[-]p70[-]p71[-]p72[-]p73[-]p74[-]p75[-]p76[-]p77[-]p78[-]p79[-]p80[-]p81[-]p82[-]p83[-]p84[-]p85[-]p86[-]p87[-]p88[-]p89[-]p90[-]p91[-]p92[-]p93[-]p94[-]p95[-]p96[-]p97[-]p98[-]p99[-]p100[-]p101[-]p102[-]p103[-]p104[-]p105[-]p106[-]p107[-]p108[-]p109[-]p110[-]p111[-]p112[-]p113[-]p114[-]p115[-]p116[-]p117[-]p118[-]p119[-]p120[-]p121[-]p122[-]p123[-]p124[-]p125[-]p126[-]p127[-]p128[-]p129[-]p130[-]p131[-]p132[-]p133[-]p134[-]p135[-]p136[-]p137[-]p138[-]p139[-]p140[-]p141[-]p142[-]p143[-]p144[-]p145[-]p146[-]p147[-]p148[-]p149[-]p150[-]p151[-]p152[-]p153[-]p154[-]p155[-]p156[-]p157[-]p158[-]p159[-]p160[-]p161[-]p162[-]p163[-]p164[-]p165[-]p166[-]p167[-]p168[-]p169[-]p170[-]p171[-]p172[-]p173[-]p174[-]p175[-]p176[-]p177[-]p178[-]p179[-]p180[-]p181[-]p182[-]p183[-]p184[-]p185[-]p186[-]p187[-]p188[-]p189[-]p190[-]p191[-]p192[-]p193[-]p194[-]p195[-]p196[-]p197[-]p198[-]p199[-]p200[-]p201[-]p202[-]p203[-]p204[-]
{% endccb %}

This was also noticeable before the cleanup, with a long string of `>[-]` repeated many times.

Loops in brainfuck repeat until the value at the current pointer is 0. So `[-]` decreases the value until it is 0. This segment appears to delete information (which may be valuable) from most of the memory.

Upon looking closer, we realize that there are many such segments in the code. So we take only the code until the first such segment, and run it in the compiler.

{% ccb caption:code wrapped:true scrollable:true %}

{% endccb %}

Output:

![Wrong! is in the memory](/static/BlahajCTF2023/brainfix_1.PNG)

We see that the characters in `Wrong!` are contained in cells 56-61.

Upon searching for `p56` in our corrected code, we end up at this segment:

{% ccb wrapped:true scrollable:true %}
p55[-]p51[p54+p55+p51-]p55[p51+p55-]p54[p53[-]p54[-]]p51[p56[-]+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p57[-]++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p58[-]+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p59[-]++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p60[-]+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p61[-]+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++p62[-]+p63[-]+p64[-]p66[-]p67[-
{% endccb %}

Notice that there is a `p51[` before the characters are created using long chains of `+`s. We can reasonably guess that if we make cell 51 to be 0, `Wrong!` will not be created, and so nothing will be output.

Also, from some random testing, if we input `b`, which is the first letter of `blahaj`, nothing is output.

The first letter of the flag is the second letter of the alphabet, how convenient

#Getting the flag

So it seems that when our input is correct, cell 51 will have a value of 0. Now we take the segment of code before the loop that creates `Wrong!` and run it with no input.

It appears that segment has too many open brackets, so we use more python code to tell us how many close brackets we should add

{% ccb lang:py scrollable:true gutter1:1-8 %}
counter = 0
text = ""
for i in range(len(text)):
    if (text[i] == "["):
        counter += 1
    if (text[i] == "]"):
        counter -= 1
print(counter)
{% endccb %}

After actually running the code:

![b is in the memory](/static/BlahajCTF2023/brainfix_2.PNG)

Unfortunately, cell 51 is simply `1`, but fortunately, the challenge setter was kind enough to leave the character we need, `b` in cell 3.

# Strategy

We realize that the program repeats these 2 segments - the creation of `Wrong!` and the deletion of information - many times, once per character.

Because running the segment of the program before `Wrong!` is created gives us 1 character, we only need to keep running larger segments of the program until we get the full flag.

# Strategy if we were smart

Besides the chain of `+`s that creates `Wrong!`, there is another chain of `+`s that creates a character in the flag in cell 3. The easier solution is to just count how many `+`s there are in each segment.


`blahaj{bf_15_7uR1nG_c0mPL3tE}`
